- [x] **p26.56 import: store a non-USD split's native amount from the FOREIGN (fdb/fcr) columns, not the base (db/cr) columns.** Data-corruption fix. The importer derived every split's native amount from `NetDebit(r.Db, r.Cr, exp)` (transactions.go `resolveSplit`, campus.go `recordAmount`) but posted it with `currency = r.Currency`. In the export `db`/`cr` carry the org-BASE (USD) figure and `fdb`/`fcr` the FOREIGN (native) figure (docs/ledger-export.md "Amounts": `Fdb // foreign … authoritative`), so every non-USD (HNL) split was stored with its USD magnitude MISLABELED as HNL native; reports then converted that already-USD figure HNL→USD a SECOND time, shrinking HNL balance-sheet accounts ~24× (on the xrt≠1 subset). A NEW `nativeNetDebit(r, exp, base)` helper (parse.go) selects the column pair by currency: `db/cr` when `r.Currency == cfg.BaseCurrency`, else `fdb/fcr`. Both amount call sites use it; `NetDebit(db,cr,exp)` stays a tested low-level primitive. The branch is REQUIRED, NOT "uniform fdb/fcr": on the real export `db != fdb` on a large fraction of BOTH USD splits (their foreign HNL counterpart lives in fdb) AND HNL splits (their base USD counterpart lives in db), so a uniform column choice corrupts one side — a USD/non-USD branch is mandatory. MULTI-CURRENCY safety: the importer buckets by `r.Currency` and balances each currency bucket independently through FX Clearing WITHOUT ever consulting `xrt` to relate legs, so switching a bucket's legs to their native pair keeps each bucket self-balancing (0 store rejections). Tests (synthetic, rule 11): `TestNativeNetDebitSelectsColumnPairByCurrency` (a non-USD split with `db≠fdb` stores the fdb figure; a USD split with a ~24× foreign fdb stores the db figure) and `TestForeignSplitStoresNativeAndConvertsForReport` (an MXN split stores its MXN native from fdb/fcr, the drawdown pool converts that native MXN→USD correctly, and a single-currency non-USD txn nets to zero) — both proven to FAIL under the old db/cr path and pass after; the campus fixture's tid-12 foreign row was corrected to the real export convention (base in db/cr, native in fdb/fcr — the one row where the fixture's third convention diverged in value). Real-data verify (counts/figures only, rule 11, temp `bin/dev-hnl.db`, NOT committed): `cuento check` clean, 0 store rejections; the four vetted HNL balance-sheet targets now tie EXACTLY as-of 2021-12-31 (Pledges Receivable-HNL 12,754.89, Petty Cash Blue Bag 4,500.99, Banco Occidente 2 292.08, Banco Atlantida 61.25 — were ~24× too small); USD accounts UNCHANGED (Land 166,482.00 exact); FY2021 total revenue 1,081,291.31 (income statement unchanged, no regression). `go vet ./...` / `gofmt -l` (empty) / `make test` / `make check` green.

- [x] **p26.58 ux: discard an in-progress reconciliation (soft status, audit intact).** A "Discard" action on the OPEN workspace soft-abandons the recon per RULE 14 (NO hard delete). New status value `discarded` via migration `00023` — SQLite cannot ALTER a CHECK, so the reconciliations table is REBUILT (create with `CHECK (status IN ('open','finalized','discarded'))`, copy, drop, rename). Because `splits.reconciliation_id` is an FK INTO reconciliations and `Open()` sets `foreign_keys=ON`, the DROP would trip that FK; the migration is `-- +goose NO TRANSACTION` (goose runs it on one `*sql.Conn`) and toggles `PRAGMA foreign_keys` OFF/ON around the rebuild (the runner's pre-migration backup covers the lost atomicity, rule 4). The `trg_split_locked_when_finalized` trigger (ON splits, references reconciliations) blocks the DROP by name, so it is DROPped first and RECREATED verbatim against the rebuilt table. `discarded` is free everywhere: every predicate keys on `status='open'` (CountOpenReconciliations / reconList / WorkspaceSplits) or `status='finalized'` (opening chain / Z9 / FinalizedReconciledSplitIDs), so a discarded recon is excluded from ALL of them automatically — `ErrOpenReconciliationExists` passes (a fresh recon can start), the list drops the Continue link, and Z9 ignores it. Store `DiscardReconciliation` guards `status='open'` (`ErrReconciliationNotOpen`), then in ONE change: UN-clears the recon's splits (`reconciliation_id -> NULL`, new `UnclearReconciliationSplits` query — LIVE-ONLY per 00014, so NO split version and the finalized-lock trigger never fires since the recon is still open) and flips status to `discarded` with a versioned op='update' snapshot. NO row is deleted anywhere (recon/versions/changes all remain), and un-cleared splits drop out of Z8 — `make check` stays clean. Web `reconDiscard` handler (POST `/reconciliations/{id}/discard`, TxnWrite, routes.go) redirects to the list on success (non-open → clean 409). Template: a discard form on the open workspace; a discarded recon renders read-only (rows use `or Finalized Discarded` as the read-only gate) with a `recon.discarded_note`. New i18n `recon.discard`/`recon.discarded_note` (both catalogs). Tests: store `TestDiscardReconciliation` (AssertVersioned op='update'; split released with NO new split version; recon+version rows survive; the open-recon guard now lets a fresh recon start and re-clear the released split; ledger clean) + `TestDiscardReconciliationValidation` (finalized → ErrReconciliationNotOpen, missing → NotFound); web `TestReconDiscardReleasesAndRemovesFromList` (gone from the continue list, start form returns, split uncleared, fresh start via the list POST). e2e (reconcile.spec): start → clear a split → discard → (a) gone from the continue list / start form back, (c) a fresh recon starts, (b) the split is uncleared/available in the fresh workspace. `go vet ./...` / `gofmt -l` (empty) / `make test` / node `--test` / i18n parity / `make check` (fresh-migrated-db clean) / reconcile e2e green.

- [x] **p26.67 import: guard the reverse-convention FX edge case (Caja Moneda Extranjera).** A second-pass reconciliation found ONE `default_currency=USD` account (Caja Moneda Extranjera, 5 rows in the dataset) stored in LEMPIRA instead of USD. The p26.56 base branch (`nativeNetDebit` → `db/cr` when `currency == base`) assumes the documented base invariant (`xrt = 1`, `db == fdb`); these rows violate it — `xrt ≈ 24.8`, `db/cr` holds the lempira figure and `fdb/fcr` the true USD. A NARROW guard (`reverseConventionBaseRow`) detects exactly the violated invariant — `currency == base` AND `xrt != 1` AND both net-debits nonzero and unequal AND the base magnitude is the LARGER one equal to the foreign magnitude scaled by xrt (`|net(db,cr)| == |net(fdb,fcr)| * xrt`) — and takes native from `fdb/fcr`. Verified against the real export: matches precisely those 5 rows / 1 account and NO other row (normal USD rows keep the smaller USD side in `db/cr`, so the `|base| > |foreign|` clause fails). Synthetic tests: a reverse row stores fdb/fcr; a normal base row (`db==fdb`, `xrt=1`) and a normal USD row (USD in `db/cr`, larger foreign in `fdb/fcr`) are unchanged; reverse debit/credit balance. `go vet` / `gofmt -l` (empty) / `make test` / `make check` green.

- [x] **p26.68 reports: fix Capital Campaign Capitalized + RNA lines (route through FundPeriodStatement).** A report-vs-py reconciliation found two internal inconsistencies in the p26.51 Capital Campaign report: (1) the Capitalized COLUMN netted fund LIABILITY splits into itself (`q.capitalized -= r.Amount`) while the detail section listed only ASSET accounts — so the column could not be reconciled from the rows shown; (2) RNA accumulated as an independent spendable-asset balance instead of its documented formula `Rev − Exp − Capitalized`, double-counting a construction liability. Root cause: the report re-implemented fund classification inline instead of using the shipped p15.8 `FundStatement`. Fix: `runCapitalCampaign` now derives every line from `FundPeriodStatement` (Gross Revenue=Received, Gross Expenses=AppliedExpense, Capitalized=Capitalized, RNA=Closing) over per-quarter [qFrom,qTo] for flows and [start,qEnd] for balances. `FundStatement.Capitalized` is asset-only (its CapitalAccounts set) and the detail lists exactly those accounts, so the Capitalized COLUMN == the detail SUM by construction; and since the fund opens at 0, `Closing == Received − AppliedExpense − Capitalized`, which is exactly the RNA formula (a liability draw routes to Received, not Capitalized, keeping it clean). Fixture `ExtendCapitalCampaign` gains a construction-loan liability financing a purchase (DR Construction / CR Loan, no cash leg) so the bug is exercised: golden moves (Gross revenue now carries the loan proceeds, Capitalized stays asset-only, cumulative RNA == Rev − Exp − Capitalized). Verify-by-stash confirms `TestCapitalCampaignColumnReconciles` FAILS on the old inline code (column ≠ detail by the loan; RNA ≠ formula) and passes on the new. Tests: column==detail + RNA==formula on the report's emitted table; the existing bridge test to FundPeriodStatement. `go vet` / `gofmt -l` (empty) / `make test` / node `--test` / `make check` / reviewed `make golden` diff / report e2e green.

- [x] **p26.70 reports: present the intercompany residual as a Cumulative Translation Adjustment (CTA) equity line.** The balance sheet appended a bare footnote "Intercompany accounts do not net to zero: $X" (`compute.go` `IntercompanyNet`, rendered in `balance_sheet.go`), which on real data grows $43k→$95k→$101k and reads as a scary error though it is mostly a legitimate ASC-830 FX translation adjustment (retranslating accumulated foreign intercompany balances at the closing rate) plus a stable real-imbalance core. New toolkit method `Toolkit.IntercompanyResidualSplit` (compute.go) decomposes the residual, converted to the target, into `Closing` (IntercompanyNet valued at the as-of closing rate) and `Historical` (the SAME intercompany positions valued FLOW-wise month-by-month at each transaction's-date rate — a new path modeled on `IntercompanyNet` because `Activity` EXCLUDES intercompany accounts on a consolidated scope; a coarse `earliestICYear` yearly scan bounds the month walk so it is not decomposed from 1900). CTA = Closing − Historical (the translation component); the reconciling difference = Historical (→ 0 once the import cutoff fix lands). SCOPED to the intercompany residual (not a full ASC-830 CTA across all translated balances — noted in DECISIONS). The balance sheet's converted (single-target) view now reclassifies the residual into a **Cumulative Translation Adjustment** net-asset line and a **Intercompany reconciling difference** line, CARVED OUT of the without-restriction figure so the net-assets total (the plug) and the identity `assets == L + NA` are UNCHANGED (the added deltas sum to exactly zero: +closing restore, −(closing−historical) CTA, −historical reconciling — a contra-equity presentation, the residual REDUCED the plug). The per-currency NATIVE view (no single rate) keeps the residual as the reconciling-difference line only. New i18n `reports.balance_sheet.na.cta` + `.na.ic_reconciling` (both catalogs). Tests: `TestBalanceSheetCTASplit` (converted MXN residual — bare warning GONE, A==L+NA exact, CTA+reconciling reclassify the whole closing residual with no value lost, without moved toward its undistorted value); toolkit `TestIntercompanyResidualSplitSameCurrency` (USD residual → CTA 0, all historical) + `TestIntercompanyResidualSplitTranslation` (MXN residual → nonzero CTA, Closing/Historical == ConvertMinorAt at the two dates); the native warning test updated to the reconciling label. - [x] **p26.71 reports: align functional-expenses + 990 Part IX to transaction-date FX (so Part IX ties the income statement).** A reconciliation found the functional-expenses total and 990 Part IX total did NOT equal the income statement's total expenses when intra-year FX rates move (real-data FY2025 gap ~$5,034.66): the income statement converts expense FLOWS at the transaction-date rate (`RateTxnDate`) but functional-expenses (`functional_expenses.go`) and 990 Part IX (`form_990.go`) converted at the single period-end CLOSING rate — and within form_990 revenue (txn-date) and expenses (closing) sat on different bases. Now FE grand total == income-statement total expenses == 990 Part IX grand total EXACTLY, regardless of intra-year FX. - [x] **p26.72 import: config-driven manual adjustment entries (+ the year-end cutoff correction).** A general, config-driven MANUAL ADJUSTMENT capability: a new `corrections` list on the importer config (`Config.Corrections`, `[]Correction` in `mapping.go`) holding fully-specified, self-balancing journal entries the mechanical CSV import cannot express — e.g. a year-end IN-TRANSIT transfer whose sending leg posts one fiscal year (US books) and whose receiving leg posts the next (Honduras books), which cuento otherwise mis-TIMES. Each `Correction` is one transaction (`date`, `subsidiary` name, `currency`, optional `memo`/`description`, and `splits`); each `CorrectionSplit` names an `account` (source_acct), an EXACT signed net-debit `amount` (int64 minor units, Dr +/Cr −, never a float or the lossy source `v`, rule 3), and optional `fund`/`program`/`functional_class`/`description`. `builder.corrections` (`corrections.go`) runs in `runBuild` AFTER every subsidiary's transactions, resolves the human-readable keys against the id maps the import already built, and posts through `PostTransaction` — so an adjustment is versioned (rule 5) and passes every ledger invariant (rule 7: single currency+subsidiary, per-transaction AND per-fund zero-sum, program-on-R/E-only, class-on-expense-only). UNLIKE a source group it gets NO synthesized plug leg: it MUST already balance, so a residual is a LOUD build failure (naming the offending correction), never plugged. The SPECIFIC cutoff values live ONLY in the gitignored `fixtures/source/mapping.json` (rule 11): TWO HNL entries on the Honduras (UPH) books — at FY2021 close, Cr the intercompany revenue account `Donaciones del Exterior` (both the income account AND the D19 receiving leg, so one credit recognizes FY2021 income and drops the intercompany residual) with the receiving program on the revenue leg (rule 7), Dr Opening Balances as the in-transit counter; then the exact REVERSE at the FY2022 receipt date so the real receiving leg does not double-count (all-time net zero; only the timing shifts). Amount is the EXACT integer from tid 23486's native HNL figure (not the lossy CONS `v`). Synthetic tests (rule 11): `TestCorrectionPostsBalancedAdjustment` (a `corrections` entry posts a balanced fund-tagged correction with the exact integer amounts/accounts/program; ledger.Check Error-clean) + `TestCorrectionRejectsUnbalanced` (a non-zero-sum correction fails the build loudly). - [x] **p26.82 ops: auto-reset for hosting the public demo + deploy docs.** A mechanism so the hosted demo REGENERATES itself on an interval (visitors edit freely, but every reset wipes back to the pristine synthetic set). Chose the simplest ROBUST approach — an EXTERNAL systemd timer that regenerates the file + restarts the server — over an in-process db swap, because the running server holds an open connection pool AND live scs sessions over the SQLite file, so swapping the file underneath it is fragile; stop→rewrite→start is trivially correct (DECISIONS p26.82). Three new `deploy/` units mirroring the existing `cuento.service` / `ratesync.*` style: **`cuento-demo.service`** serves the demo db from a DEMO-ONLY data dir (`/var/lib/cuento-demo`, never a real one) with the FULL production hardening + security posture — it does NOT set `CUENTO_DEV` (rule 13, so the demo keeps Secure cookies); **`cuento-demo-reset.service`** (Type=oneshot) does `systemctl stop cuento-demo` → `cuento demo -o …/cuento.db -force` (as the cuento user; `-force` overwrites the file + its `-wal`/`-shm`, so each reset is pristine) → `systemctl start cuento-demo`; **`cuento-demo-reset.timer`** fires it (`OnBootSec=15min`, `OnUnitActiveSec=1h`, tunable). The generation is deterministic + OFFLINE (no network), so a reset is fast and cannot hang; the demo needs neither Litestream (nothing to back up — it regenerates from code) nor the ratesync timer (rates are seeded synthetically). `docs/deploy.md` gains §9 "Hosting the public demo": the never-point-at-real-data warning, the demo login credentials table (sourced from the `synth` constants so it can't drift), and the generate→serve→auto-reset walkthrough; `docs/cli.md` documents the `cuento demo` command + flags and lists it in the command table (with a note that local-only `devseed` is intentionally omitted from the deploy reference). Verified the `-force`/refuse behavior end-to-end (refuse-existing exits 1, `-force` overwrites exits 0) and RENDER-SMOKED the generated demo: `serve -dev` + login as `admin`, all 13 reports return HTTP 200 with substantive rows at root/consolidated scope (form_990 40 rows, functional_expenses/income_statement populated, capital_campaign shows "Restore the Way" with Land/Construction/Capitalized, converted consolidated balance sheet renders the full net-assets breakdown) — the first time all four seams compose, so this proves requirement (a). NO-JS: the Run button (report) and Apply button (accounts/register) stay in `<noscript>` and the plain `method="get"` form still submits on Enter/click with a full reload. Chrome-only (goldens render the reports-package Table/CSV, not the page shell — unchanged). No new i18n (the report Run button reuses `reports.params.run`). DECISIONS p26.90 (records the report-only `hx-push-url` divergence + `hx-sync` on every form). Tests: Go `TestReportResultsFragmentSwap` (the fragment renders bare — no shell, no form — with a fresh CSV href reflecting the request params); e2e reports.spec migrated off the removed Run button (render tests navigate the equivalent GET) + a new spec asserting an as-of DATE change auto-applies with no submit button, refreshes the CSV href, persists on reload, and settles latest-wins on two rapid changes (it drives the as-of control at the scope-base currency so the swap needs NO exchange-rate conversion — the fresh test db has no rates, and picking a non-base target currency would legitimately 500, unrelated to this chrome). `go vet ./...` / `gofmt -l` (empty) / `make test` / `make check` / reports+accounts+register+csp-clean e2e green.

### Pre-release audit fixes (integrity-critical cluster; added 2026-07-17)

- [x] **p26.91 store: reject a duplicated existing split id in UpdateTransaction (`ErrDuplicateSplitID`).** An UpdateTransaction input carrying the SAME existing split id twice (different amounts) passed the overall zero-sum check together but the update loop applied `UpdateSplit` twice to the one live row (last-write-wins), persisting an UNBALANCED set the zero-sum check could not catch. Fix: a seen-set over the existing split id in `validateAndResolve` (gated on the update path, `liveAccountByID != nil`) rejects the second occurrence with a NEW typed sentinel `ErrDuplicateSplitID` BEFORE any write, so the change rolls back with no audit trace. Negative store test `TestUpdateDuplicateExistingSplitIDRejected` replays the worked case `[{id:5,amt:100},{id:5,amt:300},{id:6,amt:-400}]`, asserting `errors.Is(err, ErrDuplicateSplitID)`, an unchanged change count (no trace), and that the live splits stay the original balanced 100/300/-400 set. `go vet` / `gofmt -l` (empty) / `make test` / `make check` green.

- [x] **p26.92 ledger: add a Z3 tamper/orphan guard for `user_report_grants`.** `user_report_grants` is a live, store-written, versioned composite-membership table (entity_id=user_id, snapshot group_name) like `account_subsidiaries`/`fund_subsidiaries` — each of which gets a full Z3 block — but it was MISSING from Z3, so a tampered or orphaned grant went undetected by `cuento check` (an authorization-integrity gap: a grant added by DB tampering, or a live grant with no version snapshot, passed clean). Fix: a UNION ALL Z3 block mirroring `account_subsidiaries` — (1) membership-vs-latest-snapshot keyed on (user_id, group_name), flagging `v.id IS NULL OR v.op='delete'`, and (2) the dangling-snapshot guard (latest version op<>'delete' with no live row). The Z3 SQL is the reviewed `const sqlZ3` (rule 6 exception for the static integrity checks), so no sqlc `.sql.go` sync. Sibling negative test `TestZ3TamperedGrant`: a real report group (FK-valid) + a live grant inserted with NO version row (FKs on, so only Z3 fires) is flagged Z3; `TestCheckValidWorldClean` still clean. `go vet` / `gofmt -l` (empty) / `make test` / `make check` green.

- [x] **p26.93 money: reject int64 overflow in `Parse` instead of silently wrapping.** `parseDigits` accumulated `v = v*10 + d` with no guard, and the `intVal*scale + fracVal` combine could overflow, so a 20+ digit amount string (which reaches `Parse` from raw HTTP-form text in transactions/budgets/reconcile/expenses with no upstream length cap) silently WRAPPED to a bogus in-range value — a rule-3 exactness hole. Fix: (1) a `maxAmountDigits = 18` cap in `parseDigits` rejects an over-long digit run BEFORE accumulation wraps; (2) a checked `intVal*scale` (division round-trip) + checked add for `fracVal` at the combine catches an in-range-integer-times-scale overflow — both returning the clean `parse amount %q: out of range` the func's own contract promises. Tests: `TestParseOverflowMessage` pins the out-of-range message for both the digit-cap and scale-combine paths and asserts an 18-digit boundary value still parses (no false rejection); two overflow rows added to `TestParseRejectsMalformed`. `go vet` / `gofmt -l` (empty) / `make test` / `make check` green.

- [x] **p26.94 reports: capital classification scans the fund's cumulative position, not just the window.** `FundPeriodStatement` built its CAPITAL-asset set (asset accounts a fund capitalized into, excluded from spendable Opening/Closing) from IN-WINDOW rows only, so a report window starting AFTER a capitalization mis-classified the held asset as "cash" and OVERSTATED spendable Opening (and thus Closing) by the asset's opening balance. Fix: PASS 1 now scans the fund's cumulative rows up to the window end (`date <= to`, already the `FundLedger(f, to)` bound) to build the capital set; the `[from,to]` restriction is removed. `capital_campaign.go` benefits automatically. GOLDEN CHECK: the shipped goldens use cash-only / full-inception windows where the two classifications coincide, so `make golden` is BYTE-IDENTICAL (verified: `-update` changed only `compute.go`, zero golden files); no golden NUMBER moved. Regression test `TestFundPeriodStatementPreWindowCapitalExcluded` (fixture Building Fund capitalizes Building 2025-06-15; a 2025-07-01.. window classifies Building as capital and reports spendable Opening/Closing 1,000,000, not the buggy 5,000,000). DECISIONS p26.94 (the classification-is-cumulative choice + zero-golden rationale). `go vet` / `gofmt -l` (empty) / `make test` / `make check` green.

- [x] **p26.95 web: report currency conversion with no exchange rate returns a CLEAN inline error, not a 500.** A report converting to a target currency with no rate on file (`store.ErrRateMissing` from `rep.Run`) hit `s.serverError` → 500; under apply-on-change (p26.90) htmx does NOT swap a 5xx, so the filter silently did nothing. Fix: `reportPage` catches `errors.Is(err, store.ErrRateMissing)` and renders a localized `reports.error.no_rate` (naming the currency) in the `#report-results` region with HTTP 200, via a shared `renderReportResults` helper (same swap logic as the success path; table + CSV suppressed on error). CSV export keeps its visible 500 (a download error is not silently swallowed). New i18n key in both catalogs. Tests: Go `TestReportMissingRateInlineError` (fragment 200 + inline message, no table/CSV; was a 500 before) + e2e `converting to a rate-less currency shows an inline error, not a 500` (seed USD posting, select MXN, assert swap 200 + `.report-error`). DECISIONS p26.95. `go vet` / `gofmt -l` (empty) / `make test` / `make check` / reports+csp-clean e2e green.

- [x] **p26.96 chore: audit-cluster trivial cleanups (behavior-neutral).** Bundle of five behavior-neutral fixes from the audit: (1) `store/expense_reports.go` ConvertExpenseReport — dropped the redundant `status=="converted"` branch (the following `status!="submitted"` already returns the same `ErrExpenseReportState`). (2) `store/balances.go` RegisterPage text filter now routes through the existing `likeContains` helper (like descriptions.go) so a literal `%`/`_` in the register search matches itself instead of acting as a LIKE wildcard. (3) `web/routes.go` `grantChecker` gains a `u.IsAdmin` short-circuit (returns the always-false closure) so an admin ReportGroup request skips a wasted `ReportGrants` query — behavior-neutral because `decide()` allows admins via its `u.IsAdmin` short-circuit BEFORE the grant closure is ever consulted (verified), and the closure fails closed anyway. (4) `money/date.go` `parseFlexibleDate` — doc-comment note that `strings.FieldsFunc` ignores empty separator-delimited fields (accepted hand-typed leniency); comment-only, parse behavior unchanged. (5) `money/date_test.go` — replaced the hand-rolled `stringsContains`/`containsInput` with `strings.Contains`. `go vet` / `gofmt -l` (empty) / `make test` / `make check` green.

- [x] **p26.97 store: the reconciliation seam reads splits via sqlc, not raw string-literal SQL (rule 2/6).** `synth.ExtendReconciliation` (shipped in the binary via `cuento demo`) enumerated the clearable Checking US / USD splits with a raw string-concat SQL query on a threaded `*sql.DB`, violating rule 2 (reads via sqlc only) / rule 6 (no string SQL), with unspecified row order. Fix: add sqlc query `SplitsByAccountCurrency` (`:many`, splits by account + txn currency on non-deleted txns, `ORDER BY s.id`) + exported `Store.SplitsByAccountCurrency` (`[]AccountSplitRef{ID, TransactionID}`); the seam calls the store and takes no DB handle. Dropped the `queryer` interface + the `*sql.DB` threaded through `BuildDemo`/`ExtendReconciliation` and its fixture + CLI callers. Hand-synced `internal/db/sqlc/transactions.sql.go` (2-param `...Params` + `...Row` structs, skeleton copied from `SubsidiaryNativeTotals`; sqlc not installed). Also resolves the ORDER-BY determinism nit. Behavior-neutral: demo anti-drift (BuildDemo→ExtendReconciliation→new query, check-clean + deterministic) + fixture recon tests pass unchanged (clearedCount oracle unaffected). New store test `TestSplitsByAccountCurrency` (currency filter + id ordering). DECISIONS p26.97. `go vet` / `gofmt -l` (empty) / `make test` / `make check` green.

- [x] **p26.98 i18n: add two live-missing template keys + a preventive template-key scan test.** `import_queue.tmpl` rendered `{{t "import.col.payee"}}` and `funds.tmpl` rendered `{{t "funds.view_statement"}}`, but NEITHER key existed in either catalog — so users saw the raw key strings (rule 9 leak). `TestCatalogParity` is parity-only (en vs es) and cannot catch a key absent from BOTH. Written test-first: it flagged EXACTLY the two keys above, then went green once both were added. - [x] **p26.99 i18n: pre-build Localizers eagerly; drop the per-call mutex.** `localizer(lang)` took a package-global `sync.Mutex` on EVERY call (incl. cache hits), serializing all i18n lookups. Fix: build both language Localizers inside `bundle()`'s `sync.Once` (iterating `Langs()`) and store them in `localizers`; `localizer()` now does a lock-free read of the never-mutated map, and `localizeMu` is removed. An unknown lang (not in `Langs()`) falls back to the pre-built base (`en`) Localizer — same English text as the old on-demand `[lang, en]` localizer (verified by `TestFallbackToEnglish` under `-race`). (2) `import_preview.tmpl` — added a one-line comment marking the `{{define "import-preview"}}` fragment as LEGACY/tests-only (the live upload UI renders `import-map-preview`; this define is reached only via `importPreview`'s `hasLegacyColumnFields` branch the handler already labels tests-only). The PIPED/scripted path (pipe/file/non-terminal — every test + the `printf … | cuento user add` flow) is byte-for-byte UNCHANGED. Minimal footprint: pinned `x/term@v0.43.0` (compatible with the existing `x/sys v0.45.0`, no `x/sys` bump), promoted indirect→direct via `go mod tidy` (go.mod +1 require line, go.sum +2 hash lines). New `TestReadPasswordPipedPath` locks the non-terminal branch; existing piped-password tests pass unchanged. DECISIONS p26.108; PLAN D15 updated. `go vet` / `gofmt -l` (empty) / `make test` / `make check` green.

- [x] **p26.109 ux: the live imbalance chips render fund NAMES + localized labels, not English literals / a raw fund id (rule 9).** `txneditor.js` `recompute()` rendered the overall chip with a hardcoded `'total'` and each per-fund chip with `fmtChip(k || 'unrestricted', …)` where `k` was the fund DATABASE ID — so users saw `total: …` and `5: …` instead of localized text and the fund name. Fix (server-stamp labels + read names from the DOM): the form now carries `data-chip-total="{{t "txn.total"}}"` and `data-chip-unrestricted="{{t "txn.fund.unrestricted"}}"` (new `txn.total` key in both catalogs; `txn.fund.unrestricted` already existed), and `recompute()` reads those labels + resolves each per-fund key to its NAME via a new pure `chipLabel(key, names, unrestrictedLabel)` helper in `txnfund.js`. DEVIATION FROM THE AUDIT (recorded here): rather than stamp fund id→name pairs as a JSON `data-*` (a novel, zero-precedent pattern that risked a rule-12 nit), the names are READ from the fund `<select>` options — proper nouns the server already rendered there (rule 9), the SAME DOM-reading pattern `markSubsidiaryConflicts` already uses in this file. Amount formatting stays client-side. `chipLabel` is node-tested (unrestricted→label, known id→NAME, unknown id→raw-id fallback so the chip never blanks). New e2e (txn-editor) posts a two-fund imbalance and asserts the chips show `Alpha Grant:` / `Beta Grant:` + a `Total:` label, never a bare `\d+:` id. node --test (124 pass) + txn-editor + csp-clean e2e green; the p26.98 template-key scan self-guards the new `data-chip-total` key. No golden impact (chips are client-side). `go vet` / `gofmt -l` (empty) / `make test` / `make check` green.

- [x] **p26.110 web: fix the p26.98 template-key scan's comment-strip regex (it hid real `{{t}}` refs).** The comment-stripping regex `\{\{-?/\*.*?\*/-?\}\}` did not allow whitespace around the trim markers, so it failed to close a comment ending in `*/ -}}` (a space before the trim dash — used in base.tmpl) and the lazy `.*?` BLED forward to the next spaceless `*/}}`, swallowing everything in between and hiding those lines' `{{t}}` refs from the scan (e.g. `shell-nav`'s keys between two comments). The item-3 guarantee ("asserts EACH referenced key resolves") was therefore not fully met. Fix: `\{\{-?\s*/\*.*?\*/\s*-?\}\}` (whitespace tolerated on both sides — handles `{{/*`, `{{- /*`, `*/}}`, `*/ -}}`, `*/ }}`). Proven empirically: a temporary `{{t "zzz.bogus.probe"}}` inserted into the previously-over-matched span PASSED under the old regex (bug) and FAILED (flagged) under the new one (coverage), then removed. Test-only change. `go vet` / `gofmt -l` (empty) / `make test` / `make check` green.

## Phase 27 — Budget redesign: retire schedules, cash-flow-first split-derived budgeting (added 2026-07-17 per user; DESIGN listed, UNTICKED future work)

Retires the Phase-19 schedule-based budget model and replaces it with cash-flow-first, *split-derived* budgeting: a budget becomes a set of projected, dated splits (ledger-shaped, but stored in a budget-scoped table so actuals stay clean), with an implicit unnamed "cash available" counter-leg. See DECISIONS "Budget redesign — retire schedules, cash-flow-first split-derived budgeting (added 2026-07-17)" for the full design + rationale + the three surfaced tensions (per-fund breakout vs aggregate cash; A/R–A/P inflow/outflow direction; `optional program` vs D24/Z15). All steps below are FUTURE work — left UNTICKED. **Sequence this AFTER the pre-release audit's pivotal fixes land** (do not interleave a schema-retiring redesign with in-flight go-live corrections). Same working method as every phase: tests first, implement to green, `make lint test check`, tick + commit per step.

- [x] **p27.1 db+store: shared account attributes `current_cash` + `open_item`.** Add two boolean columns to `accounts` (+ the `accounts_versions` twin, rule 5) in ONE forward-only migration: `current_cash` (spendable-cash marker, used as the cash-flow projection's opening base) and `open_item` (A/R–A/P open-line marker — shares this step because both are one-column + versioned-store + form-field + `cuento check`-awareness; splitting them duplicates the plumbing). Thread both through the versioned store write/read + the account create/edit form + the account option/tree models; `cuento check` gains any invariant the flags imply (e.g. `current_cash` only on asset accounts). **Dependency note:** the A/R–A/P *feature* built on `open_item` (aging, settlement) is separate future work — this step ships only the shared *attribute*. **This is the shared prerequisite** for both the budget redesign (needs `current_cash`) and the separately-planned A/R–A/P work (needs `open_item`). *Split into 27.1a (schema + versioned store + `cuento check` + demo) and 27.1b (account form + chart labeling) so the schema/store hand-sync surface lands green before the form.*
  - [x] **p27.1a db+store: migration + versioned store + `cuento check` + demo.** Migration `00027` adds `current_cash` + `open_item` (INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0) to `accounts` and the nullable twin columns to `accounts_versions` (00008 default-program ripple precedent), plus INSERT/UPDATE trigger backstops (`current_cash` asset-only; `open_item` asset/liability-only). Hand-synced the sqlc account models/queries (GetAccount, InsertAccount, UpdateAccount, InsertAccountVersion — appended LAST, physical order). Store: `CreateAccountInput`/`UpdateAccountInput` carry the flags; `CreateAccount`/`UpdateAccount`/`DeactivateAccount` write + version them; validation via `ErrCurrentCashNotAsset` / `ErrOpenItemBadType` (mirrors `ErrFunctionalClassNotExpense`), enforced in the store AND a new `cuento check` rule **Z20** (Error). Z3 accounts block extended. Demo/synth flag representative accounts (Checking US/MX current_cash; Due-from receivable + Due-to payable open_item) + anti-drift asserts ≥1 of each. Negative store tests + Z20 tests.
  - [x] **p27.1b web: account create/edit form + chart labeling.** Two checkboxes ("Current cash account" / "Open-item (A/R–A/P)") with server-enforced type-gating (shown only for the eligible types via new `IsAsset`/`IsAssetOrLiability` conditionals + the existing htmx type-refetch); the store rejects a wrong-type flag (handler maps `ErrCurrentCashNotAsset`/`ErrOpenItemBadType` to a field key at 422, surfaced even when the gated control is hidden). New i18n keys both catalogs (labels + errors + A/R–A/P badges). Light chart labeling: `open_item` threaded through the tree query (2nd sqlc hand-sync) → an `open_item` asset shows an "A/R" badge, a liability an "A/P" badge. Handler negative test (equity + open_item → 422) + positive create test (flags stored, badge shown) + e2e (type-gating hides/shows the controls, A/R badge on the chart).
- [x] **p27.2 db+store+import: budget-splits table + entry/import + cadence helper.** New budget-scoped table `budget_splits(id, budget_id, desc, date, account_id, fund_id NULL=unrestricted, program_id NULL, amount INTEGER minor, currency)` + a versioned `_versions` twin (rule 5) — NOT the real `splits`/`transactions` ledger (actuals stay clean). A budget-split is single-legged (the balancing "cash available" counter-leg is IMPLICIT and UNNAMED, per the design); budget-splits are a separate projection plane and are NOT subject to the ledger's per-transaction / per-fund zero-sum invariants. Store CRUD through the funnel; validation reuses D20/D24 (fund/program/sub exist; program prefilled/required on R/E-categorized legs, optional only for A/L — resolves DECISIONS tension 3). A **cadence helper** (pure, deterministic, no clock, no stored object) generates dated rows weekly/biweekly/monthly from a start date — pure entry/import sugar that materializes rows and forgets (the key simplification replacing the retired schedule concept). Flat-CSV import `[desc, date, account, fund, optional program, amount]` → budget-splits (mirrors the org's spreadsheets). Web: budget-split entry grid (reuses the phase-12/expense-grid pieces) with the cadence helper + the CSV import. *Split into 27.2a–e (schema+store+check → cadence helper → entry UI → CSV import → demo) so the versioned two-table plumbing lands green before the UI (like p27.1a/b). Naming: the container is `budget_plans` (NOT `budgets`, which stays live until p27.3 retires it); the split FK is `plan_id`; `subsidiary_id` lives on the PLAN (leaf check resolves against `plan.subsidiary_id`); the physical desc column is `description` (SQL-keyword avoidance).*

Clock-free, DOM-free, materialize-and-forget (NO stored schedule object). node-test covers weekly/biweekly/monthly, the month-end clamp (incl. leap Feb), year-boundary, and bad-input → []. Browser glue dispatches a `budget:cadence` event carrying the dates; the grid module (p27.2c) consumes it to clone the row.

## Phase 28 — Two-row split-grid polish (added 2026-07-18 per user; post-v1 UI polish batch)

Chrome-only polish of the three two-row split-entry grids (transaction editor, expense-report grid, budget-plan grid) so they read consistently. No behavior/number changes; goldens unchanged. Same working method: adjust tests first where a layout assertion pins the old shape, implement to green, `make test check` + relevant e2e, tick + commit per step.

- [x] **p28.1 ux: unify the two-row split grids (error/delete on row 1, memo/amount to the edge, stacked headers, non-red totals, themed notes).** Across all THREE grids (txn `transaction_form.tmpl`+`txneditor.js`, expense `expense_detail.tmpl`, budget `budget_plan_detail.tmpl`): move the per-row ERROR cell + delete-× to the END of ROW 1 (after amount/account) and pin those two columns narrow via a `<colgroup>` (`col.txn-col-util`, ~2.25rem) so delete is a tight utility cell, not a full grid band; extend the trailing ROW-2 field to the right edge (memo on txn/expense, amount on the memo-less budget grid); give the expense + budget grids the SAME stacked two-line `<thead>` the txn grid has (row-1 field over row-2 field: Description/Fund, Account/Program, Amount/Memo on expense; Description/Fund, Date/Program, Account/Amount on budget) — new `budget_plan.split.col.fund`/`.program` keys in BOTH catalogs, expense reuses existing `expense.line.col.*`; drop the inter-split `tbody + tbody` top-border rules (the p26.32 per-split zebra already demarcates them — kept, and extended to `.bs-row` which previously lacked it); `memo` inputs get `autocomplete="off"` (all three); recolor the txn totals/imbalance chips NEUTRAL by default (`--color-surface`/`--color-text-muted`, not the red error token) and always show the running Total chip, flipping to danger only on a genuine imbalance (`.imbalanced`); theme the transaction-level Notes textarea (input tokens: border/radius/surface/padding, ~5-line min-height, ~60ch max-width). - [x] **p28.2 ux: fuzzy + hierarchy on EVERY account picker.** Every site where an ACCOUNT is selected is now the SAME fuzzy combobox (`combo-input`) whose option label carries the dotted HIERARCHY path (`data-path`), so a query like `c.boa` ranks `Cash.BOA` — the entry grids already had it; this adds the GAPS the owner named plus the others found: the **merge** source/destination (`#mg-src`/`#mg-dst`, `merge_form.tmpl`), the **account-ledger report** account filter (`#rp-account`, `report.tmpl`), the account-form **parent** picker (`#af-parent`, `account_form.tmpl`), and the **import** target (`#import-account`, `import.tmpl`). Reachability: the grid editors init their own combos, so a shell-wide `combos.js` (mirroring `datefield.js`: `DOMContentLoaded` + `htmx:afterSwap` → `initCombos(document)`, idempotent, skips the manual payee combo) enhances these non-grid pickers, loaded in `base.tmpl`. `acctOption`/`leafOption`/`ParentOption`/`importAccountOption` gained a `Path` (+ `Type` on `acctOption`). - [x] **p28.3 ux: Enter AND Tab both select the highlighted suggestion and advance — in the combobox AND the description field.** A new PURE key-decision helper `combokey.js` `comboKeyAction(key,{open,hasActive})` (node-tested, `combokey.test.js`) is the single source of truth: when the suggestion list is OPEN with a HIGHLIGHTED item, Enter → `{commit, preventDefault, focusNext}` and Tab → `{commit}` (native Tab advances); otherwise both fall through (a closed-list Enter still reaches the grid's save handler). `combobox.js` (account/fund/program) folds its old Enter branch + a new Tab branch through the helper and gained an `onAdvance(select)` opt; the txn editor passes `advanceComboFocus` (reuses the `gridCols`/`gridIsVisible` model to focus the NEXT visible cell, skipping `visibility:hidden` program/class). `descfield.js` folds Enter+Tab through the same helper: Enter commits + `stopPropagation`s + advances via a new `ctx.advance(input)` (focuses the row's account select — the cell that always follows the description in every grid); Tab commits and lets native/grid Tab advance (no preventDefault, so the blur reconcile then prefills from the committed full text). Reachability guard: the shell-wide `combos.js` now uses `enhance()` directly and SKIPS combos inside a grid form (`#txn-form`/`#expense-grid-form`/`#budget-grid-form`) so the editors' `onAdvance`-carrying enhancement always wins (order-independent). p26.44 keyboard bridge + p26.31 blur-timer intact. No new i18n strings. e2e (`combo-account-fuzzy.spec.js`): Enter- and Tab-selects-and-advances on an account combo, AND Enter- and Tab-selects-and-advances on the description field. green-bar: `go vet`, `gofmt`, `make test check`, `node --test`, combo-account-fuzzy/entry-keyboard/combo-descprefill/txn-editor/expense-submit/payee-autofill e2e.

- [x] **p28.4 ux: totals-red only on OVERALL imbalance (include the main balancing split).** In the transaction editor the bottom "Total" chip went red whenever the BODY splits didn't sum to zero — but with the main-split design the header/main split auto-balances the body (its amount is the residual −(body sum)), so a genuinely-balanced transaction still showed a red total. A new PURE helper `txnfund.js` `overallImbalance(bodyTotal, mainPresent)` (node-tested: `mainPresent → bodyTotal + −bodyTotal = 0`; flat grid → the body sum stands) folds the main split in; `txneditor.js` recompute detects the header via `#txn-main-header` and drives BOTH the Total chip text and its `.imbalanced` (red) state off `overallImbalance` — so in the normal editor the chip is always neutral and reads `Total: 0.00`, while the flat fallback grid (import / expense-review / multi-fund; no main split) is byte-identical to before (red on a nonzero body sum). The per-fund chips are untouched (a per-fund D20 violation legitimately stays red even when the overall nets zero). No new i18n strings; no report golden number moves. e2e (`txn-editor.spec.js`): a balanced main-split txn renders a neutral (non-`.imbalanced`) Total reading `Total: 0`, and the main-amount previews the −40 residual. green-bar: `go vet`, `gofmt`, `make test check`, `node --test`, txn-editor/entry-keyboard/combo-descprefill/combo-account-fuzzy/expense-submit/merge e2e.

Matching a leaf reveals its ancestors + type header (hierarchy still reads); matching a parent reveals its subtree (the parent name prefixes every descendant path). Collision-free with `treetable.js` (which owns `tr.hidden`): the module toggles a `searching` class on the table + `search-visible` on rows, and CSS author `display` rules win over the `[hidden]` UA rule while searching; emptying the box drops `searching` and treetable's collapse state governs again (restored for free). ### Group F — the date input as ONE reused component (added 2026-07-18 per owner: "date inputs need to be components created once and reused, rather than recreated each use")

- [x] **p28.18 ux: extract ONE `{{define "datefield"}}` partial and reuse it at all 8 sites.** The `input.js-datefield` markup was hand-written and drifting at eight sites (`report.tmpl` rp-from/rp-to, `register.tmpl` reg-from/reg-to, `reconcile.tmpl` recon-edit-date, `reconciliations.tmpl` recon-date-{id}, `budget_plan_detail.tmpl` cadence-start + per-row bs-date-{i}, `transaction_form.tmpl` txn-date). A new `templates/datefield.tmpl` `{{define "datefield"}}` (dot = a `dateFieldModel`, built by the `datefield` template func in `datefield.go` following the `makeRegRowCtx` constructor-func convention: positional id/name/value/placeholder/class/format/autofocus) emits the canonical markup — `type="text"`, `class="js-datefield …"`, `autocomplete="off"`, and OMITS name/value/placeholder/data-date-format when empty so each site reproduces exactly (cadence-start keeps no name/value; report from/to keep no placeholder). Autofocus is a caller-computed bool (three sites tie it to their own error state). The enhancer (`static/datefield.js`) is unchanged — it keys on `input.js-datefield`, so behavior is identical; report's lone `inputmode="numeric"` (which blocks `/` `-` on mobile keypads, hurting separator entry) was dropped, not baked canonical. green-bar: `go vet`, `gofmt`, `make lint test check`.

- [x] **p28.19 ux: `=` is an alias for `+` in the date shortcuts.** Owner: "make '=' same as '+'". `datefield.js applyShortcut` folds `=` into the `-`/`+` day-shift case (the unshifted key on the same physical cap, so a forward day needs no Shift); the forward direction is now `key === '+' || key === '='` so `=` shifts FORWARD (not backward via the old `key === '+' ? 1 : -1` fall-through), and it keeps the same mid-typing-literal guard so `=` stays a literal separator while a partial date is being typed. `datefield.test.js` proves `=` and `+` behave identically across a complete/empty/US value AND the mid-typing null case. green-bar: `go vet`, `gofmt`, `make lint test check`, `node --test`.

- [x] **p28.20 ux: make the shared date-field enhancer clone-safe (kills the duplicate-calendar quirk at source).** Root cause: `budgetgrid.js reEnhanceDates()` clones a row whose date input was ALREADY enhanced (so the clone carries a copied `.datefield-wrap` span + pick button + popover, minus their listeners), deletes `dataset.dfWired`, and dispatches a synthetic `htmx:afterSwap` — forcing `datefield.js enhance()` to WRAP IT AGAIN, yielding a nested second wrap + a duplicate 📅 button. Fixed in the SHARED component, not the grid: `enhance()` keeps its `dfWired` early-return first (protects the normal already-live re-scan), then — before building — if the input already sits in a `.datefield-wrap` it lifts the input out and removes the stale clone-copied wrap, so it always builds exactly ONE fresh wrap/button/popover. Invariant: one date input → one wrap → one pick button, however many times enhance runs or the row is cloned. `budgetgrid.js` is unchanged (it already strips dfWired + dispatches). Seam note: the wrapping logic lives in the Node-guarded DOM half (no jsdom dep), so the invariant is proven in e2e, not the pure node test — `budget-plans.spec.js` fills row 0 (auto-appending a cloned trailing row) and asserts each `.bs-date-cell` has exactly one `input.js-datefield` / `.datefield-wrap` / `.datefield-pick`; verified the assertion FAILS (2 wraps) without the fix. green-bar: `go vet`, `gofmt`, `make lint test check`, `node --test`, budget-plans e2e.

- [x] **p28.21 ux: date inputs "not wider than needed" (reports filters especially).** Owner: "not wider than needed (reports filters need tweaking)". A date field carries a fixed ~10-char payload (YYYY-MM-DD / MM/DD/YYYY), but only the two filter bars had a width cap (`.subnav-filters` + `.app-subnav-controls .report-params`, 8rem) — everywhere else (notably the transaction/budget grid cells) the `.js-datefield` input STRETCHED to fill its wide table cell/column (measured: txn-date 257px). A general `.js-datefield { width: 8rem; max-width: 100% }` rule (app.css) sizes every date input to its content; widthed on the INPUT not the wrap (widthing the wrap squashes the pick button, per the p26.8 note), and the inline-flex wrap gets `max-width: 100%` so it hugs input+button and never stretches. Verified: report/register filters stay snug at 128px, txn-date drops from 257px to a snug 160px (floored by the pre-existing `.txn-header .txn-field input` min-width, no clip), value never clips. Screenshot of the report filter row (snug dates + calendar) to `bin/datefield-p28.png` (gitignored throwaway). CSS only. green-bar: `go vet`, `gofmt`, `make lint test check`.

- [x] **p28.22 ux: fold the report As-of date into the shared date component too (the stretched filter the owner meant).** The `#rp-asof` filter input (`report.tmpl`, shown on balance-sheet / trial-balance) was a hand-written date input that had drifted OUT of the `js-datefield` family — no enhancer, and (lacking the class) no width cap, so it rendered STRETCHED full-width (measured 257px) while its sibling from/to were snug at 128px: exactly the "reports filters need tweaking" the owner flagged. Converted it to `{{template "datefield" (datefield "rp-asof" "asof" .AsOf ...)}}` like the other eight sites, so it now carries `js-datefield` (gaining the calendar popover + GnuCash shortcuts it was missing) and the p28.21 width cap (now a snug 128px with the pick button, consistent with from/to). Dropped its lone `inputmode="numeric"` for the same mobile-separator reason as from/to. green-bar: `go vet`, `gofmt`, `make lint test check`, reports e2e.

## Phase 29 — Visual date selector polish (added 2026-07-18 per owner)

### Group A — calendar popover: month-nav bug, month/year navigator, select-all-on-focus

- [x] **p29.1 ux: fix the calendar prev/next month arrows (they never changed the month).** Root cause: the ‹/› nav handlers call `render()`, which does `pop.textContent = ''`, DETACHING the just-clicked button; the click then bubbles to the module `closeOnOutsideClick` document listener whose `!wrap.contains(evt.target)` is now true (the target is a detached node) → it HIDES the popover, so the month re-rendered and instantly closed. Fixed at source in `closeOnOutsideClick`: a click whose `evt.target` is no longer connected to the document (`!evt.target.isConnected`) is treated as "an in-popover control consumed it" and does NOT close — one guard covering every in-popover re-rendering control (also unblocks p29.2's navigator). Proven by e2e (the pure node tests can't see DOM behavior): a new `datefield.spec.js` walks months both directions asserting the title text steps AND the popover stays visible (fails without the guard: popover vanishes). green-bar: `make lint test`, `node --test`, datefield/budget-plans/reconcile/reports e2e.

- [x] **p29.2 ux: clicking the month/year title opens a month+year navigator inside the popover.** The header center becomes a button toggling a MONTH+YEAR picker view in the same popover: a grid of the 12 localized month names (reused from `calData().months`) plus ‹ year › stepping; picking a month+year returns to the day grid on that month. Keyboard-accessible (arrows + Enter, Escape closes) like the day grid. Reuses `shiftMonth` (year step = `shiftMonth(view, ±12)`); no new pure logic. New aria-labels (`cal.choose_month`, `cal.prev_year`, `cal.next_year`) added to BOTH catalogs + stamped on `<body>` + read in `calData()`. e2e (`datefield.spec.js`) opens the navigator, steps the year, picks a month, asserts the day grid lands on the chosen month.

- [x] **p29.3 ux: selecting a date field selects all its content.** On focus, `input.select()` the whole value so typing replaces it. GOTCHA handled: a plain `focus → select()` is undone by the click's `mouseup` deselecting (so it would only work on Tab, not a mouse click); a one-shot flag set on focus + `preventDefault()` on the first `mouseup` after focus preserves the selection for a mouse click too. e2e proves both Tab-in and click-in fully replace the value on type.

### Group B — two unrelated small fixes (chart filter bar; drop the always-zero txn total)

- [x] **p29.4 ux: chart-of-accounts filters mirror the reports filter bar, and the fuzzy search moves into the toolbar.** The `accounts-controls` filter form now renders through the shared `.report-params`/`.report-field` markup (label-above-control columns, same label typography/spacing as the reports bar) instead of the old inline-label `.subnav-filters`; the subsidiary select reuses `.report-scope-select` (18rem cap under `.app-subnav-controls`, p28.29) so a full subsidiary name shows, while the type/active controls keep the default cap. The EPHEMERAL fuzzy search (`chartsearch.js`, id `#acct-search`) MOVED from the page body into the second-nav toolbar, as a SIBLING of the filter `<form>` (never a descendant) with NO `name`/session key/route — so it can neither serialize into nor fire that form's `change`-trigger GET; it stays purely client-side and resets on navigation, exactly as before. The form KEEPS its own htmx wiring (swap `#accounts-results`, `hx-sync`, no-JS submit + updating cue) and does NOT inherit the reports form's `hx-push-url`. Added a `.report-params .check` rule (the active-only checkbox lost `.subnav-filters` styling) + an `.accounts-subnav` flex wrapper; updated the subnav-render Go test to the new class. No new i18n keys. `make lint test check`, accounts e2e (incl. the ephemeral-search spec) green.

- [x] **p29.5 ux: drop the always-zero overall Total line from the transaction entry form.** A transaction is enforced zero-sum per fund AND overall (D20 + the balancing main split takes the residual), so the overall Total display was always 0 — redundant. Removed the `<span id="txn-total-overall">` from `transaction_form.tmpl` (+ its dead `data-chip-total` attr), the overall-chip block + `overallImbalance` import from `txneditor.js`, the `overallImbalance` helper + its tests from `txnfund.js`/`txnfund.test.js`, the now-unused `txn.total` key from BOTH catalogs, and the `.txn-total-chip` CSS. KEPT: the per-fund imbalance chips (which FUND is off), the `#txn-totals-error` server-error slot, the `#txn-main-amount` residual preview, and all submit-time validation (the store still rejects a non-balanced txn — only the redundant DISPLAY goes). Scope: the txn form only — the expense-report and budget-plan grids (NOT zero-sum) are untouched. Updated `txn-editor.spec.js`: the `:648` "neutral Total" test retitled/trimmed to guard only the surviving residual preview; the per-fund-chips test's overall-chip assertion swapped for a `toHaveCount(0)`; the per-fund-chips + no-account-blocked tests otherwise intact. `make lint test check`, txn-editor + entry-keyboard e2e green.

- [x] **p29.9 reports: downloaded CSVs carry a title + date-context preamble (owner request).** Every downloaded report CSV now opens with a self-describing two-line metadata header so the file is legible in a spreadsheet away from the app: line 1 = the report's localized title, line 2 = the date context (`As of, <date>` for an as-of report; `From, <date>, To, <date>` for a period report), a blank separator row, then the existing table (header + data) UNCHANGED. Emitted in the HANDLER (`reportCSV` → new `writeReportCSVPreamble`) on its own `encoding/csv` writer (so a title-with-a-comma is quoted correctly), flushed before `reports.WriteCSV` streams the table — the reports package stays i18n-free and its CSV goldens are BYTE-UNCHANGED (the preamble is handler-side). Keys on `rep.ParamsSpec` (independent `if` blocks), so a scope-only report with NEITHER as-of nor period emits just the title + blank (no date row) and a report with both emits both. Dates render in the user's date format (rule 10, via `dateFormatFor(u)`); labels REUSE `reports.params.asof/from/to` — NO new i18n keys. `reportCSV` is the only report-style CSV download (the drill-down is an HTML page; the ops backup is a raw DB file), so no other endpoint needed the change. Test `TestReportCSVMetadataPreamble` parses the body as real CSV (`FieldsPerRecord = -1` for the ragged preamble rows) and asserts title/date/table-header for both an as-of (balance sheet) and a period (income statement) report, plus a raw-body blank-separator check; the reports goldens are confirmed unchanged. `make lint test check` green.

- [x] **p29.10 web: reorder the home / "All" landing sections.** The card-grid landing (`internal/web/shell.go`) is regrouped per the owner: **Accounts** now holds accounts + reconciliations + the **Import** card (moved here, after reconciliations; the standalone Import section removed) and DROPS the funds/programs cards; **Financial** becomes its own report-only section positioned SECOND (right after Accounts) with NO nav card; **Funds** (`/funds`) and **Programs** (`/programs`) become their own sections pairing each management page with its report group folded in, both ABOVE Budget plans; Budget plans / Expenses / Personal / Admin follow; **Tax (990)** stays the lone trailing report section. ### Group D — report improvements (added 2026-07-18 per owner)

- [x] **p29.11 reports: comparative statements grow to the full viewport width.** The monthly/quarterly Statement of Activities (`income_statement`) and the per-program Program statement (`program_statement`) fan into many columns; the p28.23 wide shell still capped `<main>` at `min(100rem, …)`, so a many-column matrix truncated/scrolled. Added a `WideMatrix bool` to `reports.Report` (set on those two reports — a self-documenting registry flag, NOT a Granularity-reuse: `program_statement` has no Granularity, and hardcoding slugs downstream is brittle), mirrored to `reportPageModel.FullWidth` in the handler (where `rep` is in scope) and onto a new `baseData.FullWidth` → `<main class="… app-main-full">` → a new `.app-main-full { max-width: min(100%, 100% - 2*var(--space-6)); }` layered over `.app-main-wide` (keeps the page gutter, drops the 100rem cap). Narrow reports (trial balance) leave `WideMatrix` false and keep the ordinary wide shell so they don't stretch sparsely. `TestWideMatrixReportsFullWidth` asserts income/program statements carry `app-main-full` and trial balance does not. Presentation-only: report goldens byte-unchanged.

- [x] **p29.12 web: an empty/cleared report date defaults to bracket ALL data.** For PERIOD (from/to) reports, an omitted From defaults to the day BEFORE the oldest non-deleted transaction and an omitted To to the day AFTER the newest, so a cleared bound captures everything (owner request). Added `store.LedgerDateRange(ctx) (min, max string, ok bool)` over non-deleted transactions (a `MIN/MAX(date)` sqlc query); `ok=false` (empty ledger) falls back to the prior year-start/today default. SCOPE: PERIOD from/to only (as-of defaults unchanged); GLOBAL min/max (all subsidiaries) for simplicity (DECISIONS). A report run with explicit from/to is unchanged, so period goldens that pass explicit dates stay byte-identical.

- [x] **p29.13 ux: every program selector shows the hierarchy (like account pickers).** Mirror p28.2 for programs: `store.ProgramPaths(ctx)` (program id → dotted ancestor path over the program tree), a `Path` field on the web `programOption`, stamped on every program `<select>`'s option `data-path` (+ `class="combo-input"` where a site was still a plain native select) so the shared fuzzy combobox (`combos.js`/`combofilter.js`) shows and ranks by the hierarchy. Applied at every program-select site; native no-JS `<select>` still works; the submitted value is still the program id.

- [x] **p29.15 reports: the Program statement is a collapsible, doubly-hierarchical report (owner request; REVERSES the p26.26 "OUT" note for this report).** The program statement now renders its ACCOUNT hierarchy as the shared collapsible tree (reusing the Statement-of-Activities / p26.25 treetable machinery) AND keeps the PROGRAM hierarchy in its columns. Registered `Tree: true` so `report.tmpl` emits per-row `data-depth` + the collapse/expand controls + `treetable.js`; `runProgramStatement` was restructured from a flat (account×currency) matrix into `indexTree`+`fold`+`walk` (SoA-style): placeholder-parent accounts (Revenue/Expenses, or any grouping account) emit `RowSubtotal` roll-up rows over their INDENTED child accounts; leaves stay drillable, subtotals are not (a rollup spans many leaves). **Currency-outer grouping (DECISIONS p29.15):** native mode cannot sum a mixed-currency parent into one figure, so the CURRENCY dimension is promoted to the OUTERMOST grouping — one full Revenue/Expense/Net block PER currency (sorted), within which every account is single-valued and the tree renders cleanly; the per-currency fold keeps a USD-only leaf out of the MXN block and vice-versa. Converted mode (a target currency picked) drops the Currency column and renders ONE clean tree/block. **Program hierarchy** unchanged: the columns are the programs in tree pre-order, each parent-program column already the roll-up of its descendants (`ProgramActivity`, D24) — General = org-wide total; column headers kept plain (the CSV header contract is pinned). Underlying `ProgramActivity` math, the per-cell/rollup drills, and the p27.4 program-scope row filter are UNCHANGED (presentation-only over the same computed activity). **Golden** (`program_statement.{txt,csv}`, reviewed): every LEAF figure byte-unchanged, rows de-interleaved into per-currency blocks, NEW Revenue/Expenses placeholder subtotals each = Σ its children within that currency block (MXN Expenses 8,600 = 5,000+3,600; USD Expenses 23,275 = 16,500+2,100+3,050+600+25+1,000; …); net lines per currency unchanged. Tests: `TestProgramStatementCollapsibleTree` (Tree flag; Expenses subtotal = Σ same-currency children; per-currency leak guard; subtotal not drillable; leaf indent = parent+1) and `TestProgramStatementNestedSubtotal` (inline DEEP tree — a placeholder nested UNDER Expenses at depth 1 over depth-2 leaves — proving the nested rollup = Σ same-currency children and treetable contiguity, the case the flat fixture/demo trees can't exercise); all pre-existing numeric/drill/scope/converted tests stay green unchanged. e2e (`reports.spec.js`) seeds a nested expense parent→leaf and drives collapse-all (leaf hides) / expand-all (restores) on the program statement. Demo screenshot to `bin/program-stmt-p29.png` (gitignored). `export PATH=…; make lint` (0 issues) + `make test` + reports e2e green.

- [x] **p29.16 web: transaction history as a vertical timeline of SAVED-STATE cards (owner request — the lightly-formatted `old -> new` text made it hard to see how a transaction changed).** The `/transactions/{id}/history` page is redesigned from a per-change diff list into a timeline of state CARDS (first → … → current), each showing the FULL transaction at that version (header field grid + the split rows as they stood) with the CHANGES from the prior version highlighted. The store already reconstructs per-change diffs from the append-only version twins; `store.TransactionHistory` is extended to ALSO carry each version's full reconstructed state (`HistoryEntry.State`: `HistHeaderState` + ordered `[]HistSplitState`) by CARRY-FORWARD in change order — a running header snapshot + a `map[splitID]state` walked over the ordered version rows: every split live as of a version is present (an untouched split carries forward; a removed split shows once as a `delete` ghost at its last position, then drops; void writes no split versions so its splits carry forward with the header marked Deleted). Per-row change status ("" unchanged / create / update / delete) is overlaid so the web layer can highlight what moved. The web layer (`renderHistory`) resolves ids→names (rule 9, request language) and amounts→display (rule 10, per-version currency/exponent) into `histVersionView`s. Add/remove/change are signaled by COLOR (green/red/amber) **plus** a `+`/`−`/`~` marker and a status word — color is never the only cue (a `.hist-vis-label` visually-hidden label pairs each marker for screen readers); changed header fields and split cells show the struck prior value inline. New `app.css` history block (state cards on a timeline rail, split table, `--color-warning`/`-bg` tokens added); no inline script/style (rule 12). New i18n keys (`history.intro/.legend/.was/.col.*/.seq.*/.marker.*`) in BOTH catalogs. Store tests assert the reconstructed full state: untouched split carried forward, memo-only edit keeps splits neutral (the store only versions changed splits — `splitUnchanged`), removed-split ghost-then-dropped, void carries splits. Web test asserts the state-card structure + a changed field is visibly marked. e2e (`txn-history.spec.js`) asserts two state cards, each with a full split table, and the current card marks the edited memo (struck prior value). Demo screenshot to `bin/history-p29.png` (gitignored). `export PATH=…; make lint` (0 issues) + `make test` + txn-history e2e green.
- [x] **p29.17 ux: report-oriented print CSS (owner request — a printed / saved-as-PDF report should be a clean, self-identifying, unchanging snapshot; there was essentially NO `@media print` CSS, so printing dumped the full app chrome around the table).** A `@media print` block in `internal/web/static/app.css` refits the report page for paper: (1) STRIP THE CHROME — `body > *:not(#main){display:none}` hides every chrome sibling (top nav + New-transaction + logout in `.app-header`, the second-level filter/subnav bar, footer, skip link, flash) in one future-proof rule, plus in-`#report-results` chrome (`.report-export` CSV link, `.report-controls`/`.tree-controls` collapse/expand, the `.htmx-indicator`/`.report-updating` cue). (2) SELF-IDENTIFYING PRINT HEADER — a new `.report-print-meta` block rendered in `report.tmpl` INSIDE `#report-results` (so an in-page as-of/period filter change, which swaps only that fragment, keeps the printed dates in sync — no stale snapshot), `display:none` on screen and `display:block` in print. (3) CLEAN TABLE — force the LIGHT theme by remapping the theme tokens to ink-on-white on `html[data-theme]` (out-specifies `:root`'s `light-dark()` and the per-theme `color-scheme`, later source order wins the tie), so a dark-theme user still prints black-on-white and every existing `var(--color-border)` accounting rule (subtotal top rule, total double-underline) resolves to black; `thead{display:table-header-group}` repeats the header on every page; `tr`/`.report-subtotal`/`.report-total{break-inside:avoid}` keep a row off a page seam and `break-before:avoid` discourages orphaning a subtotal/total; `@page{margin:1.5cm}`; the reading-width caps drop (`.app-main*{max-width:none}`). The `.report-scroll` max-height/overflow + sticky rules are already `@media screen`-scoped, so print is never clipped. LIMITATION (documented in AGENTS.md): a very wide comparative statement can exceed portrait width — no reliable cross-browser pure-CSS shrink-to-fit — so the user picks Landscape / "fit to page". AGENTS.md notes the print behavior in the UI/frontend section. ## Phase 30 — Report polish (added 2026-07-19 per owner)

- [x] **p30.9 reports: redesign the Budget variance report — qualified row labels, monthly columns, an instant Budgeted/Actual/Variance measure toggle, and magnitude-coded totals (owner request).** The `budget_variance` report flipped from a flat per-(bucket,key) table into a MONTHLY PIVOT: one ROW per key — the fully-qualified (dotted-path, `store.AccountPaths`) account + fund + program + currency — spread across one COLUMN per month bucket (reusing the cashflow `projectionBuckets` machinery + its verbatim-bucket-date `HeaderKey` trick, so NO per-month i18n keys), plus a trailing per-key **Total** column and per-currency grand-total rows. `WideMatrix: true` renders it full-viewport. Each month/Total cell is a new `CellMeasures` cell folding budgeted+actual+variance (exact minor units + currency + magnitude bucket); the shared text/CSV golden renderers emit all THREE compound (`B / A / V`; CSV `b;a;v`) so the golden stays RECONCILABLE (not variance-only). The **measure TOGGLE** (`.bv-measure-toggle`, a Budgeted/Actual/Variance button group) switches which measure the grid shows INSTANTLY, client-side, via three `<span>`s per cell + a table-level `data-measure` attribute (CSS show/hide) flipped by a hand-written CSP-safe ES module `budgetvariance.js` (pure `applyMeasure` node-tested; loaded on the page, re-wires on `htmx:afterSwap`) — NO server round-trip, NO client money math (rule 10, all three pre-formatted server-side). Only the ACTUAL span carries the drill `<a>` (live exactly when Actual shows — no link rewrapping). No-JS: the server stamps `data-measure="variance"` (default) + presses the Variance button, CSS shows the variance spans, the inert buttons do nothing. **COLOR:** the magnitude bucket is classed SERVER-SIDE (`reports.VarianceBucket`, pure ratio→enum, carried as `Cell.Bucket`, ignored by text/CSV like `Drill`); the web layer combines sign (over=red / under=green ramp) into a `bv-over-*/bv-under-*` CSS class on the variance span of the TOTAL cells (theme-aware `light-dark()` tokens + bold; color reinforces, never sole-carries, the number's sign). Thresholds (DECISIONS p30.9): `|variance|/|budgeted|` <10% slight, <25% moderate, else large; zero-budget-nonzero-variance = large; both-zero neutral. Variance = Actual − Budgeted convention KEPT (presentation-only over the same computed data). - [x] **p30.10 reports: three distinct total tiers on the tree statements (owner request).** The tree statements previously emitted the placeholder-parent roll-ups (Revenue/Expenses and nested parents) AND the section totals (Total revenue/Total expenses) BOTH as `RowSubtotal`, so in a single-parent chart "Total revenue" read identically to its "Revenue" parent. Added a new `RowSectionTotal` kind (`table.go`, appended in the const block between `RowSubtotal` and `RowTotal`) for the definitive SECTION figure, ranked BETWEEN the placeholder-parent `RowSubtotal` (lightest) and the grand-total `RowTotal` (strongest, double rule). Marked the section-total rows in `income_statement.go` (`totalRow` → Total revenue/expenses), `balance_sheet.go` (`totalLine` → Total assets/liabilities/net assets) and `program_statement.go` (`totalRow` → per-currency section totals) as `RowSectionTotal`; placeholder parents STAY `RowSubtotal`, grand totals STAY `RowTotal`. `functional_expenses` (a flat 990-Part-IX line list + grand total, no parent-vs-section collision) and `form_990` left as-is — neither is a `Tree:true` report (the task's scope was the tree statements), and although form_990 Part X emits `total_assets`/`total_liabilities`/`total_net_assets` like the balance sheet, they are within-Part subtotals over FLAT account lines (no placeholder-parent rollups to collide with) inside a multi-Part IRS-form facsimile, so the parent-vs-section-total ambiguity the tier resolves does not arise there — deliberate skip, keeps the 990 golden byte-stable. CSS: `.report-section-total` styled BETWEEN the two — 700 weight + a heavier (darker+thicker `--color-text-muted`) top rule + thin bottom rule + surface tint, vs `.report-subtotal`'s 600 weight + light 2px rule; the tiers rank by border weight/darkness + font-weight (not fill) so they survive @media print (which strips the background). `golden.go` `kindMarker` gained a single-ASCII `#` marker (width-1, no amount shift) so the `.txt` goldens now show three tiers (`>` parent, `#` section, `=` grand); the `.csv` goldens are UNCHANGED (CSV never encodes row kind). Goldens regenerated + reviewed: `income_statement.txt`, `balance_sheet.txt`, `program_statement.txt` — ONLY the leading marker flipped `>`→`#` on the section-total rows, every amount byte-identical. `income_statement_test.go` asserts the new `RowSectionTotal` on Total revenue/expenses, `RowSubtotal` on the Revenue/Expenses parents, `RowTotal` on the net. - [x] **p30.13 ux: adjacency-based combobox fuzzy matching (owner request).** The shared combobox filter (`combofilter.js`, used by EVERY combobox — accounts/funds/programs/payees via `combos.js`/`combobox.js`, and by `chartsearch.js` for chart-search membership) was a SCATTERED-subsequence matcher (`fp` matched `Food Purchases` via `f…p`), hard to reason about. Changed it to require ADJACENCY: the query is TOKENIZED on the `BOUNDARY` set (whitespace + `.` `-` `_` `/`) into fragments (empties dropped); EVERY fragment must be a CONTIGUOUS case-insensitive substring of the label, else the option is EXCLUDED (`scoreMatch` returns `null` — the contract `chartsearch.js` keys visibility off). So against `Food Purchases`: `foo`✓ `pur`✓ `f p`✓ `food purchases`✓ but `fp`✗; `c.boa`/`cash.boa`/`boa` still match `Cash.BOA`. Score (deterministic, node-tested): per fragment prefer a segment/word BOUNDARY occurrence over mid-word (else earliest); bonuses for boundary, leaf-segment (`boa`→`Cash.BOA` over `Cash.BOA.Payroll`), a first-fragment prefix, and left-to-right fragment ORDER; the small shorter-label tie nudge kept below the structural bonuses; ties break by original index (stable). Empty/blank AND separator-only queries → all options in original order. `combofilter.test.js` pins the owner acceptance set + regressions (dotted-path, leaf-vs-mid-word, prefix, adjacency-excludes-gappy). e2e retargeted: `combo-account-fuzzy.spec.js` queries that relied on the old scattered behavior (`fzchk`/`advsav`/`hipar.leaf`/`kbsav`/…) → contiguous fragments (`fuzz check`/`adv sav`/`hier.leaf`/`kb sav`/…, `combo-text` literal updated); `combo-program-fuzzy` (`gen.edufuzz`) + `combo-descprefill` (single-word) already contiguous, unchanged. Demo screenshot `bin/fuzzy-adjacency-p30.png` (`foo pur` → `Expenses.Food Purchases`, gitignored). JS-only pure-logic change (no entity/schema/report) → synth N/A. `export PATH=…; make lint` (0) + `make test` (incl. node) green; combo/descprefill/program e2e (17) green. DECISIONS p30.13.
- [x] **p30.14 web: retire the org-name setting; derive the display name from the root subsidiary (owner request).** The `org_settings` table had two keys — `org_name` (a barely-wired display label) and `enabled_languages`. Retired `org_name` end-to-end: dropped the `SettingOrgName` const + its reads/writes (`org_settings.go`), the `OrgName` field/load/save (`org.go`), the org-name `<input>` (`org.tmpl`), and the `org.form.name` i18n key from BOTH catalogs; `org.intro` now describes just the languages. The generic `OrgSetting`/`SetOrgSetting`/`EnabledLanguages` helpers and `enabled_languages` stay fully working. **No migration** to delete the stored key — it's a harmless key/value config row and migrations are forward-only with no down (rule 4); we just stopped reading/writing it. **Derived display name:** new store helper `RootSubsidiaryName(ctx)` returns the ROOT subsidiary's name (the single `parent_id IS NULL` node = the consolidating entity, D18/p09.1) by taking `SubTree()`'s pre-order first row — no new sqlc query.
